commit 0cc9f781eeeb98d6c0d2812145a525f5dfe27b40
Author: Doug Knight <karmix0@gmail.com>
Date:   2009-12-14 16:36:08 -0900

    move handling of escaped variables and directives to the parser
    
    Once text reaches the compiler, it is too late to parse escaped
    variables and directives.  The compiler does not know where the text
    came from, and can not determine when it should skip processing of
    escape sequences for raw blocks.
    
    Signed-off-by: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@monkeypox.org>

commit 4213bbe9856d9c33a35ed2d7d5dba1ca16472015
Author: Mike Bonnet <mikeb@redhat.com>
Date:   2009-10-16 19:52:41 -0400

    remove unnecessary encoding in the default filters, now that everything is a unicode object internally
    
    There is no longer any value in having the filters return encoded str objects,
    since they need to be decoded back to unicode before they can be combined with
    the rest of the template text (which is managed as a unicode object).  This
    patch maintains API compatibility but fundamentally changes the behavior of
    some of the filters.  RawOrEncodedUnicode and EncodeUnicode should be
    deprecated and removed from the API.
    
    Signed-off-by: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@monkeypox.org>

7	28	cheetah/Filters.py

commit 87cb61133ea9f1b53b811d534e3fae73e41c5e9a
Author: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@monkeypox.org>
Date:   2009-10-16 15:15:08 -0700

    Add Template.__unicode__() to return unicode() objects, while Template.__str__() returns encoded str() objects
    
    Per my discussion in #cheetah on IRC with mikeb@ regarding the following issue:
            https://bugzilla.redhat.com/show_bug.cgi?id=529332
    
    This, in addition to recent patches to cheetah/DummyTransaction.py should alleviate
    migration issues for users still passing a mishmash of unicode()/str() objects into
    Templates. __str__() should return a str() object, whereas __unicode__() should
    return a unicode() object.
    
    No-op the EncodeUnicode filter when it encounters a unicode() object.

1	1	cheetah/Filters.py
24	1	cheetah/Template.py
16	0	cheetah/Tests/Unicode.py

commit e354cde7e5b3d42c4ff34f451ada310a8fe558fc
Author: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@monkeypox.org>
Date:   2009-10-12 21:48:58 -0700

    Remove unnecessary dir()/set() calls in Template.__init__()
    
    When running cheetah.Tests.Performance.DynamicMethodCompilationTest
    with 100000 iterations set, Template.__init__() is the most performance
    sensitive call.
    
    Prior to this commit:
        ncalls  tottime  percall  cumtime  percall filename:lineno(function)
        100000   12.558    0.000   15.274    0.000 Template.py:1025(__init__)
    
    After this commit:
        ncalls  tottime  percall  cumtime  percall filename:lineno(function)
        100000    1.263    0.000    3.541    0.000 Template.py:1025(__init__)
    
    That code need not execute every time __init__ is called

2	3	cheetah/Template.py

commit 2e5c9bc2ff7bbb1b2496038860a120ecae15591b
Author: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@monkeypox.org>
Date:   2009-10-14 23:04:37 -0700

    Remove the encode/decode calls in DummyResponse.write()/getvalue() and take a more optimistic approach
    
    Borrowing some concepts from the "slide-compat" branch that I maintain
    for Slide, Inc. for gracefully handling less-than-ideal string-encoding
    situations (as is the case for Slide).
    
    Making DummyResponse.getvalue() optimistic in trying to u''.join() a
    list of random string (unicode, str (various encodings)) objects
    and then only on a UnicodeDecodeError, run through the "safeConvert"
    function (blech) to handle encoded str() objects

25	15	cheetah/DummyTransaction.py

1	0	CHANGES

commit 9d0b6662a2e5af8ee7e87273909a6e3c3ab22f9b
Author: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>
Date:   2009-05-12 20:04:16 -0700

    Add the prioritizeSearchListOverSelf compilerSetting to help with issue #11
    
    When instantiating a Template class, one of the keyword arguments possible is "searchList",
    if you pass "searchList={'foo' : 'bar'}" into the Template, the searchList that's looked
    over by the NameMapper during execution will look something like this:
    
            [{}, <Template object at 0xdeadbeef>, {'foo' : 'bar'}]
    
    Which can result in some collisions if you pass a key into the constructor that conflicts
    with a Template member name, with using prioritizeSearchListOverSelf=True, the searchList
    the NameMapper will look over will look instead like this:
    
            [{'foo' : 'bar'}, {}, <Template object at 0xdeadbeef>]
    
    Signed-off-by: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>

1	0	src/Compiler.py
25	14	src/Template.py

Author: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>
Date:   2009-04-13 07:40:01 -0400

    Correct failure to import Cheetah.Filters on Python 2.4.xx and 2.3.xx due to the markdown module requiring ElementTree
    
    For the tests, the Markdown test will not fail, but print an informative message. Use of the Cheetah.Filter.Markdown class
    in "real life" however will raise a big ugly exception and print out a download link for 2.4 and 2.3 users
    
    ElementTree was included in the base installation as of 2.5

    Finish up support for the #transform directive, and the Markdown filter
    
    Now you can set:
            #from Cheetah.Filters import Markdown
            #transform Markdown
    
            This is my header!
            ==================

            <h1>This is my header!</h1>

commit 57f0467dde98274a122f758b76e1f816bb015956
Author: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>
Date:   2009-03-27 15:40:14 -0700

    Correct a bug introduced in v2.1.0 that affected odd inline imports
    
    Added a regression test as well to prevent it from happening again, what basically
    was going on is that in v2.1.0 I introduced code to properly place inline imports, for
    syntax like the following:
    
            #try
                    #import cjson
            #except ImportError
                    #import simplejson
            #end try
    
    The actual bug was with blocks of code like this:
    
            #def function
                    #if $something
                            #from package import module
                            $module.do_thing()
                    #end if
            #end def
    
    Which would result in:
    
            def function(self):
                    if something:
                            import module
                            module.do_thing()
    
    Instead of the proper "from package import module" syntax.
    
    Sorted, all tests passing now.
    
    Signed-off-by: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>
    
    Conflicts:
    
            src/Tests/Regressions.py

5	5	src/Compiler.py
27	0	src/Tests/Regressions.py

commit 55613de05bfe192bc5578a53b052a3d0e23f246a
Author: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>
Date:   2009-03-25 20:55:34 -0700

    Provide a fix for the failing JPQ_UTF8_Test3, unicode templates within other templates.
    
    The basic diagnosis of the issue is that the basic filter for all generated code in Filters.py
    will properly handle encoding str() objects, as well as unicode() objects, but there is a third
    use case where one might pass a template instance (dynamic or otherwise compiled), in which case
    the conditional in Filter.filter() (line ~44) will fall through to the bottom case and just call:
            filtered = str(val) # val being the Template object
    
    For now we'll catch a failing str(val) call and try to follow up with a unicode(val) call.
    (tempted to just make the unicode(val) default internally to the Filter)
    
    Signed-off-by: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>

4	1	src/Filters.py

commit 2d72b61c956474af0784f53d2b06f0e2c5f0473f
Author: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>
Date:   2009-03-24 10:57:41 -0700

    Prioritize the template itself at the beginning of the searchList.
    
    Patch suggested by Peter Warasin <peter@endian.com> to solve an issue when using
    the RecursiveNull class in your searchList.
    
    What this will do for the majority case however is prevent searchlist variables from
    colliding with template defined variables or methods. In effect, if your template has:
    
            #def $mymethod()
                    #return 'foo'
            #end def
    
    And you pass the searchList=[{'mymethod' : lambda x: 'bar'}], the template will resolve the "mymethod"
    symbol defined in the template itself.
    
    Signed-off-by: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>

1	2	src/Template.py

commit 98ab690e4f24ccf3a07a6e82bcf982d5f611978c
Author: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>
Date:   2009-03-15 02:38:43 -0700

    Fix a regression that I introduced into the dynamic compiler code
    
    Basically in 9055e2c1cada9bd3e1bc9a946f4653a47aadf249, in order to support
    syntax like the following:
            #try
                    #import cjson
            #except ImportError
                    #import simplejson
            #end try
    
    I had to modify Compiler.py:addImportedVarNames() in order to properly
    place the inline import statements at the right position in the method body.
    
    This however, breaks dynamic compilation, particularly when using chunks such as:
            #from math import cos
    
    As a number of the dynamic compilation tests do, this causes an "import cos" statement
    to be inlined into source via Compiler.py:addImportStatement() which chops off the last
    part of the import statement and just passes "['cos']" into addImportedVarNames().
    
    Pretty gross.
    
    Signed-off-by: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>

7	2	src/Compiler.py

commit 9c0329d4636cff673e1ca8b93735a94a69827a37

    Signed-off-by: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>

2	2	src/Version.py

commit 4743028d1803c8782ae43ece99f7e0731a3ecfed
Author: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@monkeypox.org>
Date:   2009-03-15 01:43:18 -0700

    Apply the parallel compilation patch from Evan Klitzke (evan@eklitzke.org)
    
    Now cheetah-compile can spawn off multiple subprocesses to compile temlpates in parallel much like `make -j 2` will.
    
    Example usage:
            cheetah compile my-templates -R --parallel=2
    
    Signed-off-by: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>

commit 9055e2c1cada9bd3e1bc9a946f4653a47aadf249
Author: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>
Date:   2009-01-05 07:57:12 -0800

    Fix test, and correct the error cast in the compiler
    
    Cheetah markup like this:
            #try
                    #import cjson
            #except ImportError
                    #import simplejson
            #end try
    
    Will now appropriately generate this code:
            try:
                    import cjson
            except ImportError:
                    import simplejson
    
    Instead of what it previously generated:
            import cjson
            import simplejson
    
            try:
            except ImportError
    
    Signed-off-by: R. Tyler Ballance <tyler@slide.com>

commit c0f6ba9fc81a4604c82b3d62e2471f0b6cedf462
Author: hierro <hierro>
Date:   2006-06-16 20:15:24 +0000

      Core changes by MO:
        - WebSafe and the other optional filters in Filters.py now use
          RawOrEncodedUnicode instead of Filter as a base class.  This allows them
          to work with Unicode values containing non-ASCII characters.
              User-written custom filters should inherit from
          RawOrEncodedUnicode and call the superclass .filter() instead of str().
          str() as of Python 2.4.2 still converts Unicode to string using
          ASCII codec, which raises UnicodeEncodeError if it contains non-ASCII
          characters.

commit 700cd1a5ea9f77c14757ba761420b9d6c96541aa
Author: tavis_rudd <tavis_rudd>
Date:   2005-12-13 21:11:08 +0000

    - made it possible to pass the searchList in as an argument to #def'ined
      methods.  This makes all lookup that occur within the scope of that method use
      the provided searchList rather than self._searchList.  This does not carry
      over to other methods called within the top method, unless they explicitly
      accept the searchList in their signature AND you pass it to them when calling
      them.  This behaviour can be turned off with the corresponding compilerSetting
      'allowSearchListAsMethArg'
    - cosmetic changes
    - added support for a short EOLSlurpToken to supplement the #slurp directive

Date:   2002-05-06 20:19:49 +0000

    fixed parsing bug that would exit an expression if the directiveEndToken was a
    valid Python token and was found inside the directive.  E.g.:
    
    #compiler-settings
    directiveStartToken = .
    directiveEndToken = :
    commentStartToken = #
    #end compiler-settings
    
    .for a in [1,2,3,4][2:3]:
    blag
    .end for

commit 926092e903e9a9a8092945289663e51996fd4fd5
Author: hierro <hierro>
Date:   2001-11-10 20:40:56 +0000

    Made the Strip filter invoke the superclass like it should.  Added
    comment that this filter is not as useful as I thought for #filter,
    because it won't strip internal whitespace in multiline $placeholders.
    That would require splitting and stripping each line, but string.split()
    squeezes multiple blank lines, so you'd have to look for newlines
    manually and preserve them.  I didn't do that.

6	5	src/Parser.py

commit 6b729ad32de5a9f6fc7544442a5e6afad4178c96
Author: hierro <hierro>
Date:   2001-11-08 04:09:52 +0000

    Fixed Tavis' bugs. :)  Calling the superclass must be:
            output = Filter.filter(self, val, **kw)
    instead of:
            output = Filter.filter(output, **kw)
    
    There were two problems in both MaxLen.filter() and Pager.filter():
    1) 'output' didn't exist at that point; the argument is 'val'.
    2) You must pass 'self' explicitly when calling the superclass.
    
    A 'super' function has been proposed for a future version of Python,
    but AFAIK it has not been comitted to yet.

commit 8a601542023c75f7497562f807216de16ff62b2e
Author: ianbicking <ianbicking>
Date:   2001-11-05 06:38:40 +0000

    cheetah-compile now takes a new argument, '-w', which write the str()
    of the compiled servlets to .html files.  This is for easily creating
    static sites.
    
    The way -d and -R work has also been changed, so that they can be used
    in conjunction with -p and -w.  Instance variables hold the value of
    the various options, and everything is handled through .processFile()
    and .compileFile().
    
    -p now works just like the normal case, except it prints to stdout
    instead of the .py file.  It's implemented in .compileFile().
    
    At some point .compileDir() and .recursiveCompile() should be
    removed.

71	34	src/CheetahCompile.py

commit e298b4817ce9e33757cfc698f58c098b3fbc93ea
Author: tavis_rudd <tavis_rudd>
Date:   2001-08-03 21:48:34 +0000

    added support for #continue and #break in #for blocks.
    
    #for $i in range(15)
    #if $i == 10
    #continue
    $i
    #end for
    
    Note: #break and #continue will both move the indent level out one, so the
    "#end if" is not needed in the example above
